Here is the depth-first search algorithm:
```
function dfs(node, visited):
    if node in visited:
        return
    visited.add(node)
    if node == V12:
        return
    if node == V17:
        return
    for neighbor in graph[node]:
        dfs(neighbor, visited)
```
We can call this function with the initial node V12 and the initial set of visited nodes as V11. If the function returns without finding V17, then V12 and V17 are d-separated given V11.

Here is the code to implement this algorithm in Python:
```
graph = {
    'V0': ['V1'],
    'V2': ['V3', 'V7', 'V9'],
    'V3': ['V7'],
    'V4': ['V8'],
}

def dfs(node, visited):
    if node in visited:
        return
    visited.add(node)
    if node == 'V12':
        return
    if node == 'V17':
        return
    for neighbor in graph[node]:
        dfs(neighbor, visited)

visited = set(['V11'])
if not dfs('V12', visited):
    print('V12 and V17 are d-separated given V11')
else:
    print('V12 and V17 are not d-separated given V11')
```
